The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \\\"backtrace\\\" of each\\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\\n5: //! place).\\n6: //!\\n7: //! ### External view\\n8: //!\\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\\n11: //!\\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\\n14: //!\\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\\n24: //!\\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \\\"true\\\"\\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\\n39: //!   \\\"backtrace\\\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\\n43: //!\\n44: //! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\\n45: //! which includes two bits of information:\\n46: //!\\n47: //! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\\n48: //!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\\n49: //!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\\n50: //!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\\n51: //!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\\n52: //!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\\n53: //!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\\n54: //! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\\n55: //!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\\n56: //!\\n57: //! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\\n58: //! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`). This implies that\\n59: //! all obligations were either errors or returned an ambiguous result.\\n60: //!\\n61: //! ### Implementation details\\n62: //!\\n63: //! For the most part, comments specific to the implementation are in the\\n64: //! code. This file only contains a very high-level overview. Basically,\\n65: //! the forest is stored in a vector. Each element of the vector is a node\\n66: //! in some tree. Each node in the vector has the index of its dependents,\\n67: //! including the first dependent which is known as the parent. It also\\n68: //! has a current state, described by `NodeState`. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01JVJq2CQNvAZGkHAZkkCRrN","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"250: }\\n251: \\n252: struct FulfillProcessor<'a, 'tcx> {\\n253:     selcx: SelectionContext<'a, 'tcx>,\\n254: }\\n255: \\n256: fn mk_pending<'tcx>(\\n257:     parent: &PredicateObligation<'tcx>,\\n258:     os: PredicateObligations<'tcx>,\\n259: ) -> PendingPredicateObligations<'tcx> {\\n260:     os.into_iter()\\n261:         .map(|mut o| {\\n262:             o.set_depth_from_parent(parent.recursion_depth);\\n263:             PendingPredicateObligation { obligation: o, stalled_on: vec![] }\\n264:         })\\n265:         .collect()\\n266: }\\n267: \\n268: impl<'a, 'tcx> ObligationProcessor for FulfillProcessor<'a, 'tcx> {\\n269:     type Obligation = PendingPredicateObligation<'tcx>;\\n270:     type Error = FulfillmentErrorCode<'tcx>;\\n271:     type OUT = Outcome<Self::Obligation, Self::Error>;\\n272: \\n273:     /// Compared to `needs_process_obligation` this and its callees\\n274:     /// contain some optimizations that come at the price of false negatives.\\n275:     ///\\n276:     /// They\\n277:     /// - reduce branching by covering only the most common case\\n278:     /// - take a read-only view of the unification tables which allows skipping undo_log\\n279:     ///   construction.\\n280:     /// - bail out on value-cache misses in ena to avoid pointer chasing\\n281:     /// - hoist RefCell locking out of the loop\\n282:     #[inline]\\n283:     fn skippable_obligations<'b>(\\n284:         &'b self,\\n285:         it: impl Iterator<Item = &'b Self::Obligation>,\\n286:     ) -> usize {\\n287:         let is_unchanged = self.selcx.infcx.is_ty_infer_var_definitely_unchanged();\\n288: \\n289:         it.take_while(|o| match o.stalled_on.as_slice() {\\n290:             [o] => is_unchanged(*o),\\n291:             _ => false,\\n292:         })\\n293:         .count()\\n294:     }\\n295: \\n296:     /// Identifies whether a predicate obligation needs processing.\\n297:     ///\\n298:     /// This is always inlined because it has a single callsite and it is\\n299:     /// called *very* frequently. Be careful modifying this code! Several\\n300:     /// compile-time benchmarks are very sensitive to even small changes.\\n301:     #[inline(always)]\\n302:     fn needs_process_obligation(&self, pending_obligation: &Self::Obligation) -> bool {\\n303:         // If we were stalled on some unresolved variables, first check whether\\n304:         // any of them have been resolved; if not, don't bother doing more work\\n305:         // yet.\\n306:         let stalled_on = &pending_obligation.stalled_on;\\n307:         match stalled_on.len() {\\n308:             // This case is the hottest most of the time, being hit up to 99%\\n309:             // of the time. `keccak` and `cranelift-codegen-0.82.1` are\\n310:             // benchmarks that particularly stress this path.\\n311:             1 => self.selcx.infcx.ty_or_const_infer_var_changed(stalled_on[0]),\\n312: \\n313:             // In this case we haven't changed, but wish to make a change. \"report_selection_error\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Rust compiler's trait obligation fulfillment chain operates through a sophisticated multi-stage process:\\n\\n### 1. Obligation Storage and Forest (ObligationForest)\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs`\\n\\nThe `ObligationForest<O>` is the core data structure that tracks outstanding trait obligations. It maintains a tree-based structure where each obligation can have sub-obligations that must be satisfied for the parent obligation to succeed. The forest supports two main operations: registering obligations via `register_obligation()` and processing them via `process_obligations()`. The `ForestObligation` trait defines what types can be stored in the forest, while `ObligationProcessor` defines how to process them, enabling different strategies for different obligation types.\\n\\n### 2. Fulfillment Context (Old Solver)\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs`\\n\\nThe `FulfillmentContext<'tcx, E>` manages the fulfillment process using the ObligationForest. It implements the `TraitEngine` interface and is responsible for:\\n- Storing pending obligations in an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation<'tcx>>`\\n- Implementing the `FulfillProcessor` which is an `ObligationProcessor` that drives trait selection\\n- Managing the interaction between type inference and obligation resolution\\n\\nThe `PendingPredicateObligation` wraps a `PredicateObligation` and tracks which type inference variables the obligation is currently stalled on, enabling efficient re-processing.\\n\\n### 3. Trait Selection and Candidate Collection\\n**Files:**\\n- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs` - SelectionContext definition\\n- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs` - Candidate assembly logic\\n\\nThe `SelectionContext` is the heart of trait resolution. Its `assemble_candidates()` method in candidate_assembly.rs collects all possible implementations that might satisfy a trait obligation:\\n- **Trait aliases** via `assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias()`\\n- **Impl candidates** via `assemble_candidates_from_impls()` - searches the trait impl database\\n- **Caller bounds** via `assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds()` - checks where-clauses and environment\\n- **Builtin candidates** for language items like `Sized`, `Copy`, `Clone`\\n- **Project candidates** for associated types\\n- **Object, closure, generator, and function pointer candidates**\\n\\nThe `assemble_candidates_from_impls()` function performs a deep rejection check using `DeepRejectCtxt` for quick filtering, then calls `match_impl()` for each potentially applicable impl.\\n\\n### 4. Impl Matching (Pattern Matching)\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs`\\n\\nThe `MatchAgainstFreshVars<'tcx>` struct implements `TypeRelation` to perform pattern matching between obligation types and impl types. It uses fresh type variables to check if types could potentially unify without affecting the current inference state. This bidirectional matching allows the compiler to quickly determine if an impl could apply before committing to full unification.\\n\\n### 5. Candidate Confirmation\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs`\\n\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `confirm_candidate()` verifies the selection by:\\n- Confirming builtin candidates via `confirm_builtin_candidate()`\\n- Confirming impl candidates via `confirm_impl_candidate()` which performs full unification\\n- Confirming parameter candidates, projection candidates, and special candidates (closures, coroutines, etc.)\\n\\nEach confirmation may generate new sub-obligations that must also be satisfied.\\n\\n### 6. Error Reporting for Unsatisfied Bounds\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs`\\n\\nThe `TypeErrCtxt::report_selection_error()` method handles reporting when a trait obligation cannot be satisfied. It:\\n- Determines the error type (Unimplemented, Overflow, Ambiguous, etc.)\\n- Provides contextual error messages based on the obligation cause\\n- Suggests potential fixes (importing traits, fixing type annotations, etc.)\\n- Reports related trait implementations that almost matched\\n\\n### 7. Obligation Storage and Forest (ObligationForest)\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs`\\n\\nThe `ObligationForest<O>` is the core data structure that tracks outstanding trait obligations. It maintains a tree-based structure where each obligation can have sub-obligations that must be satisfied for the parent obligation to succeed. The forest supports two main operations: registering obligations via `register_obligation()` and processing them via `process_obligations()`. The `ForestObligation` trait defines what types can be stored in the forest, while `ObligationProcessor` defines how to process them, enabling different strategies for different obligation types.\\n\\n### 2. Fulfillment Context (Old Solver)\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs`\\n\\nThe `FulfillmentContext<'tcx, E>` manages the fulfillment process using the ObligationForest. It implements the `TraitEngine` interface and is responsible for:\\n- Storing pending obligations in an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation<'tcx>>`\\n- Implementing the `FulfillProcessor` which is an `ObligationProcessor` that drives trait selection\\n- Managing the interaction between type inference and obligation resolution\\n\\nThe `PendingPredicateObligation` wraps a `PredicateObligation` and tracks which type inference variables the obligation is currently stalled on, enabling efficient re-processing.\\n\\n### 3. Trait Selection and Candidate Collection\\n**Files:**\\n- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs` - SelectionContext definition\\n- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs` - Candidate assembly logic\\n\\nThe `SelectionContext` is the heart of trait resolution. Its `assemble_candidates()` method in candidate_assembly.rs collects all possible implementations that might satisfy a trait obligation:\\n- **Trait aliases** via `assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias()`\\n- **Impl candidates** via `assemble_candidates_from_impls()` - searches the trait impl database\\n- **Caller bounds** via `assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds()` - checks where-clauses and environment\\n- **Builtin candidates** for language items like `Sized`, `Copy`, `Clone`\\n- **Project candidates** for associated types\\n- **Object, closure, generator, and function pointer candidates**\\n\\nThe `assemble_candidates_from_impls()` function performs a deep rejection check using `DeepRejectCtxt` for quick filtering, then calls `match_impl()` for each potentially applicable impl.\\n\\n### 4. Impl Matching (Pattern Matching)\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs`\\n\\nThe `MatchAgainstFreshVars<'tcx>` struct implements `TypeRelation` to perform pattern matching between obligation types and impl types. It uses fresh type variables to check if types could potentially unify without affecting the current inference state. This bidirectional matching allows the compiler to quickly determine if an impl could apply before committing to full unification.\\n\\n### 5. Candidate Confirmation\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs`\\n\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `confirm_candidate()` verifies the selection by:\\n- Confirming builtin candidates via `confirm_builtin_candidate()`\\n- Confirming impl candidates via `confirm_impl_candidate()` which performs full unification\\n- Confirming parameter candidates, projection candidates, and special candidates (closures, coroutines, etc.)\\n\\nEach confirmation may generate new sub-obligations that must also be satisfied.\\n\\n### 6. process:\\n\\n### 1. Obligation Storage and Forest (ObligationForest)\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs`\\n\\nThe `ObligationForest<O>` is the core data structure that tracks outstanding trait obligations. It maintains a tree-based structure where each obligation can have sub-obligations that must be satisfied for the parent obligation to succeed. The forest supports two main operations: registering obligations via `register_obligation()` and processing them via `process_obligations()`. The `ForestObligation` trait defines what types can be stored in the forest, while `ObligationProcessor` defines how to process them, enabling different strategies for different obligation types.\\n\\n### 2. Fulfillment Context (Old Solver)\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs`\\n\\nThe `FulfillmentContext<'tcx, E>` manages the fulfillment process using the ObligationForest. It implements the `TraitEngine` interface and is responsible for:\\n- Storing pending obligations in an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation<'tcx>>`\\n- Implementing the `FulfillProcessor` which is an `ObligationProcessor` that drives trait selection\\n- Managing the interaction between type inference and obligation resolution\\n\\nThe `PendingPredicateObligation` wraps a `PredicateObligation` and tracks which type inference variables the obligation is currently stalled on, enabling efficient re-processing.\\n\\n### 3. Trait Selection and Candidate Collection\\n**Files:**\\n- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs` - SelectionContext definition\\n- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs` - Candidate assembly logic\\n\\nThe `SelectionContext` is the heart of trait resolution. Impl Matching (Pattern Matching)\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs`\\n\\nThe `MatchAgainstFreshVars<'tcx>` struct implements `TypeRelation` to perform pattern matching between obligation types and impl types. It uses fresh type variables to check if types could potentially unify without affecting the current inference state. This bidirectional matching allows the compiler to quickly determine if an impl could apply before committing to full unification.\\n\\n### 5. Candidate Confirmation\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs`\\n\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `confirm_candidate()` verifies the selection by:\\n- Confirming builtin candidates via `confirm_builtin_candidate()`\\n- Confirming impl candidates via `confirm_impl_candidate()` which performs full unification\\n- Confirming parameter candidates, projection candidates, and special candidates (closures, coroutines, etc.)\\n\\nEach confirmation may generate new sub-obligations that must also be satisfied.\\n\\n### 6. Error Reporting for Unsatisfied Bounds\\n**File:** `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs`\\n\\nThe `TypeErrCtxt::report_selection_error()` method handles reporting when a trait obligation cannot be satisfied. It:\\n- Determines the error type (Unimplemented, Overflow, Ambiguous, etc.)\\n- Provides contextual error messages based on the obligation cause\\n- Suggests potential fixes (importing traits, fixing type annotations, etc.)\\n- Reports related trait implementations that almost matched\\n\\n### 7. New Trait Solver Integration\\n**Files:**\\n- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/solve/fulfill.rs` - New FulfillmentCtxt\\n- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/solve/fulfill/derive_errors.rs` - Error derivation\\n- `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/solve/select.rs` - Selection in new solver\\n\\nThe newer trait solver provides an alternative implementation with improved performance and correctness. The `FulfillmentCtxt` in solve/fulfill.rs uses the next-gen solver engine from `rustc_next_trait_solver`. The `fulfillment_error_for_no_solution()` and `fulfillment_error_for_stalled()` functions in derive_errors.rs generate appropriate error codes from solver results, including detection of higher-ranked trait bound violations and projection mismatches.\\n\\n### The Complete Chain:\\n\\n1. **ObligationForest** (`rustc_data_structures`) - stores obligation tree structure\\n2. **FulfillmentContext** (`rustc_trait_selection/fulfill.rs`) - manages overall fulfillment\\n3. **FulfillProcessor** - processes obligations through the forest\\n4. **SelectionContext** (`rustc_trait_selection/select/mod.rs`) - driven by FulfillProcessor\\n5. **assemble_candidates()** - collects candidate implementations\\n6. **assemble_candidates_from_impls()** - searches trait impl database  \\n7. **MatchAgainstFreshVars** - performs pattern matching on impl signatures\\n8. **confirm_candidate()** - validates selected candidate through unification\\n9. **report_selection_error()** - reports errors for unsatisfied bounds\\n\\nFor the newer solver path, the chain is:\\n1. **FulfillmentCtxt** (solve/fulfill.rs) - new solver's fulfillment\\n2. **SolverDelegate** - bridges to the core solver\\n3. **fulfillment_error_for_no_solution()** - derives errors from solver results\\n\\nThis design enables efficient trait resolution with good error messages while supporting both incremental obligation processing and complete error recovery.\"\n   174→}\n   175→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. The `fulfillment_error_for_no_solution()` and `fulfillment_error_for_stalled()` functions in derive_errors.rs generate appropriate error codes from solver results, including detection of higher-ranked trait bound violations and projection mismatches.\\n\\n### The Complete Chain:\\n\\n1. **ObligationForest** (`rustc_data_structures`) - stores obligation tree structure\\n2. **FulfillmentContext** (`rustc_trait_selection/fulfill.rs`) - manages overall fulfillment\\n3. **FulfillProcessor** - processes obligations through the forest\\n4. **SelectionContext** (`rustc_trait_selection/select/mod.rs`) - driven by FulfillProcessor\\n5. **assemble_candidates()** - collects candidate implementations\\n6. **assemble_candidates_from_impls()** - searches trait impl database  \\n7. **MatchAgainstFreshVars** - performs pattern matching on impl signatures\\n8. **confirm_candidate()** - validates selected candidate through unification\\n9. **report_selection_error()** - reports errors for unsatisfied bounds\\n\\nFor the newer solver path, the chain is:\\n1. **FulfillmentCtxt** (solve/fulfill.rs) - new solver's fulfillment\\n2. **SolverDelegate** - bridges to the core solver\\n3. **fulfillment_error_for_no_solution()** - derives errors from solver results\\n\\nThis design enables efficient trait resolution with good error messages while supporting both incremental obligation processing and complete error recovery.\"\n}\n","numLines":175,"startLine":1,"totalLines":175}}}
